*moment
/ˈməʊmənt ||; ˈmomənt/noun
1 [C] a very short period of time 片刻；瞬间: One moment, please (= please wait). 请等一等。 Joe left just a few moments ago. 乔刚离开不久。
2 [sing] a particular point in time （某个）时刻，时候: Just at that moment my mother arrived. 就在那个时刻，我母亲到了。 the moment of birth/death 出生╱死亡的一刻
(at) any minute/moment (now)→MINUTE¹ at the moment now 现在；此刻: I'm afraid she's busy at the moment. Can I take a message? 抱歉，她现在很忙，我可不可以记下你的口信呢？ for the moment/present for a short time; for now 暂时；目前: I'm not very happy at work but I'll stay there for the moment. 我工作得不太开心，但暂时仍然会留在那里。 in a moment very soon 立刻；马上；一会儿: Just wait here. I'll be back in a moment. 就在这里等，我一会儿就回来。 the last minute/moment→LAST¹ the minute/moment (that)→MINUTE¹ on the spur of the moment→SPUR¹

*Monday
/ˈmʌndeɪ;-di ||; ˈmʌnde; -dɪ/noun [C,U] (abbr Mon.) the day of the week after Sunday 星期一: I'm going to see her on Monday. 我星期一要和她见面。 (informal 非正式) I'll see you Monday. 我星期一和你见面。 I finish work a bit later on Mondays / on a Monday. 每逢星期一我都晚一点结束工作。 Monday morning/afternoon/evening/night 星期一上午╱下午╱傍晚╱晚上 last/next Monday 上╱下星期一 a week on Monday/Monday week (= not next Monday, but the Monday after that) 隔一个星期的星期一 The museum is open Monday to Friday, 10 till 4.30. 博物馆开放时间是星期一至星期五，上午10时至下午4时30分。 Did you see that article about Italy in Monday's paper? 星期一的报纸上有篇关于意大利的文章，你看过没有？ ☞Days of the week are always written with a capital letter. 表示星期几的词，开头字母要大写。

*moral¹
/ˈmɒrəl; US mɔ:rəl ||; ˈmɔrəl/adj
1 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) concerned with what is right and wrong 道德（上）的；与是非或对错有关的: Some people refuse to eat meat on moral grounds (= because they believe it to be wrong). 有些人因道德理由而不愿吃肉。 a moral dilemma/issue/question 道德上的难题╱问题
2 having a high standard of behaviour that is considered good and right by most people 有道德的；品行端正的；品格高尚的: She has always led a very moral life. 她一向过着很规矩的生活。 [OPP] immoral 反义词为immoral ☞Compare amoral, it has a different meaning. 与amoral比较，意思不同。
moral support help or encouragement that you give to sb who is nervous or worried 道义上的支持；精神上的支持或鼓励: I went to the dentist's with him just to give him some moral support. 我陪他一起去看牙医只是想给他一点精神上的支持。
*moral²
/ˈmɒrəl; US mɔ:rəl ||; ˈmɔrəl/noun
1 morals [pl] standards of good behaviour 道德标准: These people appear to have no morals. 这些人好像缺乏道德标准。
2 [C] a lesson in the right way to behave that can be learnt from a story or an experience 教训；寓意: The moral of the play is that friendship is more important than money. 这出戏剧的寓意是友情比金钱更重要。

morale
/məˈrɑ:l; US -ˈræl ||; məˈræl/noun [U] how happy, sad, confident, etc a group of people feels at a particular time 士气: The team's morale was low/high before the match (= they felt worried/confident). 这支球队比赛前士气很低╱很高。 to boost/raise/improve morale 鼓舞╱提高╱增进士气

moralistic
/ˌmɒrəˈlɪstɪk ||; ˌmɔrəˈlɪstɪk/adj (formal 正式) having or showing very fixed ideas about what is right and wrong, especially when this causes you to judge other people's behaviour 道德的，说教的（尤指以此来判断他人的行为）

*morality
/məˈræləti ||; məˈrælətɪ/noun [U] principles concerning what is good and bad or right and wrong behaviour 道德；道义；道德观: a debate about the morality of abortion 一场有关堕胎的道德问题的辩论 [OPP] immorality 反义词为immorality

moralize
/ˈmɒrəlaɪz; US mɔ:r- ||; ˈmɔrəlˌaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [I] moralize (about/on sth) to tell other people what the right or wrong way to behave is 说教；训诫

morally
/ˈmɒrəli ||; ˈmɔrəlɪ/adv connected with standards of what is right or wrong 与道德标准或是非观念有关

moratorium
/ˌmɒrəˈtɔ:riəm ||; ˌmɔrəˈtɔrɪəm/noun [C] a moratorium (on sth) a temporary stopping of an activity, especially by official agreement 暂停，中止（尤指根据正式协议的）: The convention called for a two-year moratorium on commercial whaling. 公约要求暂停商业捕鲸两年。

morbid
/ˈmɔ:bɪd ||; ˈmɔrbɪd/adj showing interest in unpleasant things, for example disease and death 病态的（特别对疾病、死亡等令人不快的事物感兴趣）

*more¹
/mɔ:(r) ||; mɔr/det pronoun a larger number or amount of people or things; sth extra as well as what you have 较大；更多；更大: There were more people thanI expected. 人比我预料的要多。 We had more time than we thought. 时间比我原先想象的充裕。 There's room for three more people. 还有地方再容纳三个人。 I couldn't eat any more. 我再也吃不下了。 I can't stand much more of this. 这种情况我再也忍受不了。 Tell me more about your job. 再告诉我一些有关你工作的情况。 [OPP] less or fewer 反义词为less或fewer more and more an increasing amount or number 越来越多: There are more and more cars on the road. 路上的汽车越来越多。 what's more (used for adding another fact) also; in addition （用于引入新的事实）而且，此外，更有甚者: The hotel was awful and what's more it was miles from the beach. 这旅馆极差，离开海滩又远。
*more²
/mɔ:(r) ||; mɔr/adv
1 (used to form the comparative of many adjectives and adverbs （用于构成许多形容词和副词的比较级）更) She was far/much more intelligent thanher sister. 她比她的姐姐聪明得多。 a course for more advanced students 一门为更高级的学生开设的课程 Please write more carefully. 请用心点书写。 [OPP] less 反义词为less
2 to a greater degree than usual or than sth else 更大程度地；更加: I like him far/much more than his wife. 他这个人比起他的妻子来，我喜欢得多。 [OPP] less 反义词为less
not any more not any longer 不再: She doesn't live here any more. 她不再住在这里。 more or less approximately; almost 大约；差不多: We are more or less the same age. 我们年纪差不多。

moreover
/mɔ:rˈəʊvə(r) ||; mɔrˈovɚ/adv (written 书面语) (used for adding another fact) also; in addition （用于提供另一事实）此外，而且: This firm did the work very well. Moreover, the cost was not too high. 这公司做得十分出色，而且费用也不太昂贵。

morgue
/mɔ:g ||; mɔrg/noun [C] a building where dead bodies are kept until they are buried or burned 停尸房；陈尸所 ☞Look at mortuary. 参看mortuary。

*morning
/ˈmɔ:nɪŋ ||; ˈmɔrnɪŋ/noun[C,U]
1 the early part of the day between the time when the sun rises and midday 早晨；上午；早上: Pat's going to London tomorrow morning. 帕特将于明天早上去伦敦。 Bye, see you in the morning (= tomorrow morning). 再见，明天上午见。 I've been studying hard all morning. 整个上午我都在用功。 Dave makes breakfast every morning. 戴夫每天早上都做早餐。 She only works in the mornings. 她只在上午工作。
2 the part of the night that is after midnight 午夜至日出的一段时间；凌晨: I was woken by a strange noise in the the early hours of the morning. 我在凌晨时分被奇怪的声音惊醒。 He didn't come home until three in the morning. 他凌晨三点钟才到家。
When you use the adjectives early or late before ‘morning’, ‘afternoon’ or ‘evening’ you must use the preposition in The accident happened in the early morning. We arrived in the late afternoon. With other adjectives, use on School starts on Monday morning. They set out on a cold, windy afternoon. No preposition is used before this, tomorrow, yesterday Let's go swimming this morning. I'll phone Liz tomorrow evening. What did you do yesterday afternoon? morning﹑afternoon或evening前面用形容词early或late时﹐必须用介词in﹕The accident happened in the early morning.事故发生在清晨。We arrived in the late afternoon.我们于下午较晚的时候抵达。与其他形容词连用时﹐则用on﹕School starts on Monday morning.学校于星期一早上开始上课。They set out on a cold, windy afternoon.他们在一个寒风凛冽的下午出发。前面用this﹑tomorrow﹑yesterday时则不加任何介词﹕Let's go swimming this morning.我们今日早上一起去游泳吧。I'll phone Liz tomorrow evening.明晚我会打电话给利兹。What did you do yesterday afternoon? 昨天下午你干什么来着﹖ Good morning(formal 正式) used when you see sb for the first time in the morning （早上初次见面时的问候语）早，早安 ☞In a less formal situation we just say Morning Morning Kay, how are you today? 非正式场合只说Morning：Morning Kay, how are you today?早安，凯，今天好吗？

mortal¹

2 (written 书面语) that will result in death 致命的；致死的: a mortal wound/blow 致命伤；致命的打击 to be in mortal danger 有致命的危险 ☞ Look at fatal, it has a similar meaning. 参看fatal，意思相近。

*most¹
/məʊst ||; most/det pronoun
1 (used as the superlative of many and much 用作many和much的最高级) greatest in number or amount 最大；最多: Who got the most points? 谁得分最高？ The children had the most fun. 孩子们玩得最开心。 We all worked hard but I did the most. 我们所有人工作都很努力，但我做得最多。 [OPP] least or fewest 反义词为least或fewest
2 nearly all of a group of people or things 几乎全部；大多数；大部份: Most people in this country have a television. 这个国家大部份人都有电视机。 I like most Italian food. 差不多所有意大利食品我都喜欢吃。
When most is followed by a noun which has the, this, my, etc before it, we must use most of Most of my friends were able to come to the wedding. It rained most of the time we were in Ireland. 当most后接名词﹐而名词前又有the﹑this﹑my等词时﹐必须用most of﹕Most of my friends were able to come to the wedding.我的朋友大部分都能出席婚礼。It rained most of the time we were in Ireland.我们在爱尔兰的时候﹐差不多一直下雨。 at (the) most not more than a certain number, and probably less 至多；顶多；不超过: There were 20 people there, at the most. 那里至多只有20人。 make the most of sth→MAKE¹
*most²
/məʊst ||; most/adv
1 (used to form the superlative of many adjectives and adverbs （用于构成许多形容词和副词的最高级）最) It's the most beautiful house I've ever seen. 那是我所见过的最漂亮的房子。 I work most efficiently in the morning. 我早上的工作效率最高。 [OPP] least 反义词为least
2 more than anybody/anything else 比任何人或事物都多；最多: What do you miss most when you're abroad? 你在国外的时候，最想念的是什么？ [OPP] least 反义词为least
3 (formal 正式) very 很；极；十分: We heard a most interesting talk about Japan. 我们听了一个有关日本的讲座，十分有趣。

/ˈməʊstli ||; ˈmostlɪ/adv in almost every case; almost all the time 差不多全部；大多: Our students come mostly from Japan. 我们的学生大多来自日本。

*motor¹

mould¹

2 [C] [usu.sing] a particular type 类型；性格: She doesn't fit into the usual mould of sales directors. 她可不落一般营业总监的窠臼。

/maʊnd ||; maυnd/noun[C]

2 (spoken 口语)a mound (of sth) a pile or a large amount of sth 一摞；一堆: I've got a mound of work to do. 我有一堆工作要做。

*mount¹
/maʊnt ||; maυnt/verb
1 [T] to organize sth 组织；筹备；发动: to mount a protest/a campaign/an exhibition/an attack 举行抗议；发起运动；筹备展览；发动攻击
2 [I] to increase gradually in level or amount 逐渐上升、增加或增长: The tension mounted as the end of the match approached. 比赛接近结束时，气氛越发紧张。
3 [T] (written 书面语) to go up sth or up on to sth 登上；走上: He mounted the platform and began to speak. 他走上讲台开始说话。
4 [I,T] to get on a horse or bicycle 骑上（马或自行车） [OPP] dismount 反义词为dismount
5 [T] mount sth (on/onto/in sth) to fix sth firmly on sth else 安放，安装，镶嵌（在某物之上）: The gas boiler was mounted on the wall. 煤气热水器安装在墙上。
mount up to increase (often more than you want) 增加，上升（通常比所想要的多）: When you're buying food for six people the cost soon mounts up. 要买六个人分量的食物，费用便会迅速增加。

*mountain
/ˈmaʊntən; US -ntn ||; ˈmaυntṇ/noun[C]
1 a very high hill （大）山；山岳；高山: Which is the highest mountain in the world? 哪座是世界上最高的山？ mountain roads/scenery/villages 山路；山景；山村 a mountain range 山脉
2 a mountain (of sth) a large amount of sth 大量；一大堆: I've got a mountain of work to do. 我有一大堆事要做。 the problem of Europe's butter mountain(= the large amount of butter that has to be stored because it is not needed) 欧洲大量黄油积压的问题

*move¹
/mu:v ||; muv/verb
1 [I,T] to change position or to put sth in a different position 改变位置；移动；搬动 · Please move your car. It's blocking the road. 请开走你的车，它把路给阻塞了。 The station is so crowded you can hardly move. 车站里人山人海，令人寸步难移。 The meeting has been moved to Thursday. 会议改到星期四开了。
2 [I,T] move along, down, over, up, etc to move (sth) further in a particular direction in order to make space for sb/sth else 挪动（以便腾出地方）: If we move up a bit, Rob can sit here too. 要是我们挪过去一点儿，罗布也可坐在这里。 Move your head down -- I can't see the screen. 你把头低下去，我看不见屏幕了。
3 [I,T] to change the place where you live, work, study, etc 搬家；搬迁；迁移: Our neighbours are moving to York next week. 我们的邻居下周要搬到约克去了。 to move house 搬家 Yuka's moved down to the beginners' class. 尤卡已经降到初学者的那个班。
4 [I] move (on/ahead) to make progress 取得进展: When the new team of builders arrived things started moving very quickly. 新一批建筑工人到来后，工作开始进展迅速。
5 [I] to take action 采取行动: Unless we move quickly lives will be lost. 我们不赶快采取行动的话，就会有人丧失生命。
6 [T] to cause sb to have strong feelings, especially of sadness 激起强烈情感（尤指哀伤）；感动: Many people were moved to tears by reports of the massacre. 看了有关大屠杀的报道，很多人都伤心得落泪。
get moving to go, leave or do sth quickly 快走；快离开；赶快做某事 get sth moving to cause sth to make progress 使某事有所进展 move in (with sb) to start living in a new house (with sb) 搬入，迁入（新居）；搬去与…同住 move on (to sth) to start doing or discussing sth new 开始做另一件事；改变话题 move off (used about a vehicle) to start a journey; to leave （指车辆）出发，离开 move out to leave your old home 搬出，迁出（旧居）
*move²
/mu:v ||; muv/noun[C]
1 a change of place or position 动；移动: She was watching every move I made. 她在看着我的一举一动。
2 a change in the place where you live or work 搬家；搬迁；迁移: a move to a bigger house 搬进一幢大一点的房子
3 action that you take because you want to achieve a particular result （为达成某一结果而采取的）步骤，行动，措施: Both sides want to negotiate but neither is prepared to make the first move. 双方都想谈判，但没有一方准备踏出第一步。 Asking him to help me was a good move. 找他帮我是个好办法。
4 (in chess and other games) a change in the position of a piece （棋类游戏的）一步，一着: It's your move. 该你走了。
be on the move to be going somewhere 在行进；在走动: We've been on the move for four hours so we should stop for a rest. 我们已经走了四个小时，该停下来歇一歇了。 get a move on(informal 非正式) to hurry 赶快；加紧: I'm late. I'll have to get a move on. 我迟了，得赶快一点。 make a move to start to go somewhere 动身；离去: It's time to go home. Let's make a move. 该回家了。我们走吧。

*movement
/ˈmu:vmənt ||; ˈmuvmənt/noun
1 [C,U] an act of moving 动作；活动: The dancer's movements were smooth and controlled. 那舞蹈演员的动作流畅熟练。 The seat belt doesn't allow much freedom of movement. 系上安全带以后，行动就不自由。 I could see some movement (= sb/sth moving) in the trees. 我看到树丛里有动静。
2 [C,U] an act of moving or being moved from one place to another 移动: the slow movement of the clouds across the sky 云朵在空中慢慢飘过
3 [C] [usu.sing] a movement (away from/towards sth) a general change in the way people think or behave （人们在思想上或行为上的整体）倾向，趋势，动向: There's been a movement away from the materialism of the 1980s. 20世纪80年代崇尚物质的风气已减退。
4 movements [pl] a person's actions or plans during a period of time （一个人在某段时间内的）举动，活动，计划: Detectives have been watching the man's movements for several weeks. 几个星期来，侦探一直在监视那名男子的行动。
5 [C] a group of people who have the same aims or ideas 一群有着共同目标或思想的人: I support the Animal Rights movement. 我支持动物权益运动。
6 [C] one of the main parts of a long piece of music 乐章

*much
/mʌtʃ ||; mʌtʃ/det pronoun adv
1 (used with uncountable nouns, mainly in negative sentences and questions, or after as, how, so, too 与不可数名词连用，主要用于否定句及疑问句，或用于as、how、so、too之后) a large amount of sth 大量；很多: I haven't got much money. 我没有很多钱。 Did she say much? 她说了很多话吗？ You've given me too much food. 你给我太多食物了。 How much time have you got? 你有多少时间？ I can't carry that much ! 我带不了那么多东西！ Eat as much as you can. 尽量吃吧。
In statements we usually use a lot of NOT much I've got a lot of experience. 陈述句通常用a lot of，而不用much：I've got a lot of experience.我经验丰富。
2 to a great degree 达到很大程度: I don't like her very much. 我不怎么喜欢她。 Do you see Sashi much? (= very often) 你经常和萨希见面吗？ Do you see much of Sashi? 你经常和萨希见面吗？ much taller/prettier/harder 高大╱漂亮╱困难得多 much more interesting/unusual 有趣╱奇特得多 much more quickly/happily 迅速╱快活得多 You ate much more than me. 你吃得远比我多。
3 (with past participles used as adjectives 与作形容词的过去分词连用) very 很；非常: She was much loved by all her friends. 她深受所有朋友爱戴。 ☞Compare: She was very popular. 与She was very popular比较。
much the same very similar 很相似；差不多一样: Softball is much the same as baseball. 垒球与棒球十分相似。 nothing much→NOTHING not much good (at sth) not skilled (at sth) 不善于: I'm not much good at singing. 我不善于唱歌。 not much of a... not a good... 不是个很好的…: She's not much of a cook. 她的烹饪技术不太好。 not up to much→UP

/ˈmʌltɪplaɪ ||; ˈmʌltəˌplaɪ/verb (present participle multiplying third person singular present multiplies;past tense past participle multiplied)

*murder
/ˈmɜ:də(r) ||; ˈmɝdɚ/noun
1 [C,U] the crime of killing a person illegally and on purpose 谋杀罪: to commit murder 犯谋杀罪 a vicious murder 残暴的谋杀案 the murder victim/weapon 谋杀案受害者／凶器 ☞Look at manslaughter. 参看manslaughter。
2 [U] (informal 非正式) a very difficult or unpleasant experience 十分艰难或不愉快的经历: It's murder trying to work when it's as hot as this. 在这么酷热的环境下工作，真是活受罪。
get away with murder to do whatever you want without being stopped or punished 为所欲为而不被制止或不受惩罚: He lets his students get away with murder. 他听凭自己的学生为所欲为。 ➔murder verb [I,T] ☞ Look at the note at kill. 参看kill的注释。 ➔murderer noun [C]

*muscle
/ˈmʌsl ||; ˈmʌsḷ/noun [C,U] one of the parts inside your body that you can make tight or relax in order to produce movement 肌肉: Riding a bicycle is good for developing the leg muscles. 骑自行车有助锻炼腿部肌肉。 Lifting weights builds muscle. 举重使肌肉发达。

muse¹
/mju:z ||; mjuz/verb[I]
1 muse (about/on/over/upon sth) to think carefully about sth for a time, without noticing what is happening around you 沉思；冥想: She looked out to sea, musing on what he had said. 她凝视着大海，沉思他说过的话。
2 to say sth, usually to yourself, in a way that shows you are thinking carefully about it 若有所思地说；自言自语: ‘I wonder if I should tell him?’ she mused. “我不知道该不该告诉他？”她自言自语地说。

mushroom
/ˈmʌʃrʊm;-ru:m ||; ˈmʌʃrυm; -rum/noun [C] a type of plant which grows very quickly, has a flat or rounded top and can be eaten as a vegetable 蘑菇 ☞A mushroom is a type of fungus. Some, but not all, fungi can be eaten. Toadstool is name for some types of poisonous fungi. 蘑菇是一种真菌（fungus，复数为fungi）。真菌有些可供食用，有些不可。某些种类的有毒真菌叫toadstool。

*must¹
/məst;strong form mʌst ||; məst; mʌst/ modal verb (negative must not short form mustn't /ˈmʌsnt ||; ˈmʌsṇt/)
1 used for saying that it is necessary that sth happens （表示必须）: I must remember to go to the bank today. 我今天一定要记得去银行。 You mustn't take photographs in here. It's forbidden. 你不可在这里拍照，这里禁止摄影。
2 used for saying that you feel sure that sth is true （表示肯定）: Have something to eat. You must be hungry. 吃点东西吧，你一定饿了。 I can't find my cheque book. I must have left it at home. 我找不到我的支票簿，必定是留在家里了。
3 used for giving sb advice （用于提供意见）: You really must see that film. It's wonderful. 你真的该去看看那部电影，真精彩。 ☞For more information about modal verbs, look at the Quick Grammar Reference section at the back of this dictionary. 有关情态动词的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。
must²
/məst ||; məst/noun [C] a thing that you strongly recommend 强烈推荐的事物: This book is a must for all science fiction fans. 这是所有科幻小说迷必看的书。

muster
/ˈmʌstə(r) ||; ˈmʌstɚ/verb
1 [T] to find as much support, courage, etc as you can 尽力争取（支持）；鼓起（勇气）: We mustered all the support we could for the project. 我们为这项目争取一切能争取的支持。 [SYN] summon 同义词为summon
2 [I,T] (technical术语) to come together, or bring people, especially soldiers, together, for example for military action 召集，集合（尤指士兵）: The troops mustered. 部队集合起来了。 to muster an army 召集一支军队

/mju:ˈteɪt ||; ˈmjutet/verb mutate (into sth)

2 [I] (formal 正式) to change into a new form 变成新形体: Rhythm and blues mutated into rock and roll. 节奏怨曲变成了摇滚乐。

mutual
/ˈmju:tʃuəl ||; ˈmjutʃυəl/adj
1 (used about a feeling or an action) felt or done equally by both people involved （指感受或行动）相互的，彼此的: We have a mutual agreement (= we both agree) to help each other out when necessary. 我们彼此间有个约定，就是在有需要时互相帮助。 I just can't stand her and I'm sure the feeling is mutual (= she doesn't like me either). 我就是受不了她，而我肯定她也无法忍受我。
2 shared by two or more people 共同的；共有的: mutual interests 共同兴趣 It seems that Jane is a mutual friend of ours. 简好像是我们共同的朋友。 ➔mutually /-uəli ||; -υəlɪ/ adv

muzzle

/ˈmaɪəlɪn ||; ˈmaɪəlɪn/noun [U] (technical术语) a substance that forms a covering over many of the NERVES in the body, increasing the speed at which messages travel 髓磷脂

myopia
/maɪˈəʊpiə ||; maɪˈopɪə/noun [U] (technical术语) the inability to see things clearly when they are far away 近视 ➔myopic /maɪˈɒpɪk ||; maɪˈɑpɪk/ adj [SYN]More common expressions are short-sightedness and short-sighted. 较常用short-sightedness及short-sighted。

*myself
/maɪˈself ||; maɪˈsɛlf/pronoun
1 used when the person who does an action is also affected by it （表示人受自己行为影响）我自己: I saw myself in the mirror. 我在镜子里看见自己。 I felt rather pleased with myself. 我对自己相当满意。
2 used to emphasize the person who does the action （用于强调施动者）: I'll speak to her myself. 我会亲自对她说。 I'll do it myself (= if you don't want to do it for me). 我自己会做。
(all) by myself
1 alone 单独: I live by myself. 我自己一个人住。 ☞ Look at the note at alone. 参看alone的注释。
2 without help 独自；独力: I painted the house all by myself. 我自己一个人给房子上了油漆。

*mysterious
/mɪˈstɪəriəs ||; mɪsˈtɪrɪəs/adj
1 that you do not understand or cannot explain; strange 神秘的；无法解释的；奇怪的: Several people reported seeing mysterious lights in the sky. 有几个人报称看见天空中出现神秘的光。
2 (used about a person) keeping sth secret or refusing to explain sth （指人）神秘的，诡秘的: They're being very mysterious about where they're going this evening. 他们对于今天晚上要去哪里，表现得十分神秘。 ➔mysteriously adv

*mystery
/ˈmɪstri ||; ˈmɪstrɪ/noun (plural mysteries)
1 [C] a thing that you cannot understand or explain 难以理解或无法解释的事物；神秘的事物: The cause of the accident is a complete mystery. 那宗意外的起因完全是个谜。 It's a mystery to me what my daughter sees in her boyfriend. 我想不通女儿究竟看上她男朋友什么。
2 [U] the quality of being strange and secret and full of things that are difficult to explain 神秘；神秘感: There's a lot of mystery surrounding this case. 这个案件有很多悬疑的地方。
3 [C] a story, film or play in which crimes or strange events are only explained at the end 疑案作品；推理作品

mystic
/ˈmɪstɪk ||; ˈmɪstɪk/noun [C] a person who spends his/her life developing his/her spirit and communicating with God or a god 神秘主义者（致力于发展精神境界，藉此与上帝或神沟通的人）

mystical
/ˈmɪstɪkl ||; ˈmɪstəkḷ/ (also mystic /ˈmɪstɪk ||; ˈmɪstɪk/) adj connected with the spirit; strange and wonderful 心灵的；精神的；玄妙的；不可思议的: Watching the sun set over the island was an almost mystical experience. 观看太阳在岛上西沉简直是一种奇妙的经历。

mysticism
/ˈmɪstɪsɪzəm ||; ˈmɪstəˌsɪzəm/noun [U] the belief that you can reach complete truth and knowledge of God or gods by prayer, thought and development of the spirit 神秘主义（藉祈祷、默想及发展精神境界以认识真理及上帝或神明的信仰）: Eastern mysticism 东方神秘主义

mystify
/ˈmɪstɪfaɪ ||; ˈmɪstəˌfaɪ/verb [T] (present participle mystifying third person singular present mystifies;past tense past participle mystified) to make sb confused because he/she cannot understand sth 使困惑不解；把人弄胡涂: I was mystified by the strange note he'd left behind. 我被他所留下的那张奇怪便条弄胡涂了。

mystique
/mɪˈsti:k ||; mɪsˈtik/noun [U] [sing] the quality of having hidden or secret characteristics that makes sb/sth seem interesting or attractive 神秘性

myth
/mɪθ ||; mɪθ/noun[C]
1 a story from past times, especially one about gods and men of courage. Myths often explain natural or historical events. 神话
2 an idea or story which many people believe but that does not exist or is false 假象；虚构的事物: The idea that money makes you happy is a myth. 金钱能令人快乐是一个假象。

mythical
/ˈmɪθɪkl ||; ˈmɪθɪkḷ/adj
1 existing only in myths(1) 神话的；只存在于神话之中的: mythical beasts/heroes 神话中的野兽╱英雄
2 not real or true; existing only in the imagination 不真实的；虚构的；想象的

mythology
/mɪˈθɒlədʒi ||; mɪˈθɑlədʒɪ/noun [U] very old stories and the beliefs contained in them 神话（总称）: Greek and Roman mythology 希腊及罗马神话 ➔mythological /ˌmɪθəˈlɒdʒɪkl ||; ˌmɪθəˈlɑdʒɪkḷ/ adj mythological beasts/figures/stories 神话中的野兽；神话中的人物；神话故事
